## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Compliance Audit: Envoy Access Logging Configuration Coverage

## Your Task

Audit the access logging infrastructure in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find all C++ source files under `source/extensions/access_loggers/` and `source/common/access_log/` that define access log filter implementations or access log sink implementations. Also find the corresponding `.proto` definitions in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` under `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/`. For each implementation, report whether it supports structured (JSON) logging or only unstructured text logging.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

115-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of the access logging infrastructure in Envoy v1.31.2. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

### Access Logger Sink Implementations (with JSON Support Status)

1. **File Logger** ✅ JSON - Full support for text, JSON, typed JSON, and custom formats
2. **Stream Loggers (stdout/stderr)** ✅ JSON - Supports structured formatting via SubstitutionFormatString
3. **HTTP gRPC Access Log Service** ✅ JSON - Structured via Protocol Buffers with custom tags
4. **TCP gRPC Access Log Service** ✅ JSON - Structured via Protocol Buffers  
5. **Fluentd Logger** ✅ JSON - Uses JSON formatter internally, converts to MessagePack
6. **OpenTelemetry Logger** ✅ JSON - Structured via OTLP with attributes and body fields
7. **WASM Logger** 🔧 Extensible - Format depends on WASM plugin implementation

### Access Logger Filters

Identified 12 filter implementations:
- Basic filters: StatusCode, Duration, NotHealthCheck, Traceable, Runtime
- Composite filters: And, Or
- Header, ResponseFlag, GrpcStatus, LogType, Metadata
- **CELAccessLogExtensionFilter** - Advanced CEL expression-based filtering

### Architecture Highlights

- All sink implementations inherit from `ImplBase` base class
- Consistent formatting via `SubstitutionFormatString` abstraction  
- Support for complex nested structures and custom fields
- gRPC-based loggers share common batching/buffering patterns
- Extension filter framework enables custom filter implementations

The complete findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and detailed documentation.

Overview\\nEnvoy v1.31.2 contains comprehensive access logging infrastructure spanning both sink implementations (access loggers) and filter implementations (access log filters). The system is designed to support multiple output formats, with significant JSON/structured logging support across most implementations.\\n\\n### Access Logger Sink Implementations\\n\\n#### 1. File Logger (envoy.access_loggers.file)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/file/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/common/file_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/file/v3/file.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Full support)\\n- Supports multiple format options: `format` (text), `json_format` (JSON), `typed_json_format` (typed JSON), `log_format` (SubstitutionFormatString)\\n- Implemented via `FileAccessLogFactory` which creates formatter instances using `SubstitutionFormatStringUtils`\\n- File logger writes formatted output directly to disk\\n\\n#### 2. Stream Loggers (envoy.access_loggers.stdout/stderr)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/stream/config.cc`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/stream/v3/stream.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured)\\n- Stdout/Stderr loggers support `log_format` (SubstitutionFormatString)\\n- JSON formatting possible through SubstitutionFormatString configuration\\n- Implemented via `StdoutAccessLogFactory` and `StderrAccessLogFactory`\\n\\n#### 3. gRPC Access Log Service (ALS) - HTTP (envoy.access_loggers.http_grpc)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/http_config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/http_grpc_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/v3/als.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured via Protocol Buffers)\\n- HTTP gRPC access logger sends HTTP request/response data via gRPC\\n- Supports custom tags (type.tracing.v3.CustomTag) for additional structured fields\\n- Implemented via `HttpGrpcAccessLogFactory`\\n- Proto includes HTTPRequestProperties and HTTPResponseProperties with headers/trailers\\n- Structured logging through protocol buffer messages to remote gRPC service\\n\\n#### 4. gRPC Access Log Service (ALS) - TCP (envoy.access_loggers.tcp_grpc)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/tcp_config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/tcp_grpc_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/v3/als.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured via Protocol Buffers)\\n- TCP gRPC access logger sends TCP connection data via gRPC\\n- Uses CommonGrpcAccessLogConfig with streaming and custom tags\\n- Implemented via `TcpGrpcAccessLogFactory`\\n- Structured logging through protocol buffer messages\\n\\n#### 5. Fluentd Logger (envoy.access_loggers.fluentd)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/fluentd_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/v3/fluentd.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured)\\n- Sends logs to Fluentd via Forward Protocol over TCP\\n- Uses JSON formatter internally (`SubstitutionFormatStringUtils::createJsonFormatter`)\\n- Converts JSON to MessagePack for Fluentd wire format\\n- Supports nested JSON objects through `google.protobuf.Struct record` field\\n- Configured via `FluentdAccessLogFactory`\\n- Field: `record` is a Struct containing formatted fields rendered as strings, numbers, or booleans\\n\\n#### 6. OpenTelemetry Logger (envoy.access_loggers.open_telemetry)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/open_telemetry/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/open_telemetry/access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/open_telemetry/v3/logs_service.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured)\\n- Sends logs to OpenTelemetry Logs Collector via gRPC or HTTP\\n- Structured logging via OpenTelemetry proto format (LogResource)\\n- Supports `body` (AnyValue) and `attributes` (KeyValueList) for structured fields\\n- Supports custom tags (type.tracing.v3.CustomTag) for additional attributes\\n- Implemented via `AccessLogFactory` in open_telemetry namespace\\n- Can use both gRPC and HTTP/OTLP transports\\n\\n#### 7. WASM Logger (envoy.access_loggers.wasm)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/wasm/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/wasm/wasm_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/wasm/v3/wasm.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** EXTENSIBLE (Depends on WASM plugin)\\n- Extensible logging via WASM plugin configuration\\n- Format and structure determined entirely by WASM plugin implementation\\n- Configured via `WasmAccessLogFactory`\\n- Allows custom logic for log processing and formatting\\n\\n### Access Logger Filter Implementations\\n\\nAll filters implement the `Filter` interface and are created through `FilterFactory::fromProto()` in `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.cc`. Filters are not sink implementations but determine whether logs are emitted:\\n\\n#### 1. StatusCodeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on HTTP response status code comparison\\n- Supports: GE, EQ, LE operations\\n\\n#### 2. DurationFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on request/response duration comparison\\n- Supports: GE, EQ, LE operations\\n\\n#### 3. NotHealthCheckFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters out Envoy health check requests\\n\\n#### 4. TraceableRequestFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters traceable requests only\\n\\n#### 5. RuntimeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on runtime configuration and fractional percentages\\n\\n#### 6. AndFilter / OrFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Composite filters combining multiple filters with AND/OR logic\\n\\n#### 7. HeaderFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on HTTP header matching\\n\\n#### 8. ResponseFlagFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on Envoy response flags\\n\\n#### 9. GrpcStatusFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on gRPC status codes\\n- Can infer gRPC status from HTTP status codes\\n\\n#### 10. LogTypeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on access log type (HTTP, TCP)\\n\\n#### 11. MetadataFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on dynamic metadata matching\\n\\n#### 12. CELAccessLogExtensionFilter (envoy.access_loggers.extension_filters.cel)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/filters/cel/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/filters/cel/cel.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/filters/cel/v3/cel.proto`\\n- Filters using Common Expression Language (CEL) expressions\\n- Evaluates expressions against Envoy attributes\\n- Requires USE_CEL_PARSER compile flag\\n- Supports complex filtering logic beyond built-in filters\\n\\n### Key Findings\\n\\n1. **JSON/Structured Logging Support:** 5 out of 7 sink implementations have explicit JSON support (File, Stream, HTTP gRPC, TCP gRPC, Fluentd, OpenTelemetry). WASM logger is extensible.\\n\\n2. **Formatting Infrastructure:** All sink implementations use the `SubstitutionFormatString` abstraction from `source/common/formatter/substitution_format_string.h` for consistent format handling.\\n\\n3. **Base Class Architecture:** All sink implementations inherit from `ImplBase` (in `source/extensions/access_loggers/common/access_log_base.h`), which handles filter evaluation and logging orchestration.\\n\\n4. **Filter Extensibility:** The system supports both built-in filters and extension filters via the `ExtensionFilterFactory` interface, allowing for custom filter implementations like CEL.\\n\\n5. **Common Configuration Pattern:** gRPC-based loggers (HTTP gRPC, TCP gRPC, OpenTelemetry) share common configuration patterns via `CommonGrpcAccessLogConfig` or similar structures, supporting batching, buffering, and custom tags.\\n\\n6. **Structured Data Support:** File, Fluentd, and OpenTelemetry loggers explicitly support structured data (nested objects, custom fields) through Protobuf Struct types and custom field mappings.\"\n}\n",

File Logger (envoy.access_loggers.file)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/file/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/common/file_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/file/v3/file.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Full support)\\n- Supports multiple format options: `format` (text), `json_format` (JSON), `typed_json_format` (typed JSON), `log_format` (SubstitutionFormatString)\\n- Implemented via `FileAccessLogFactory` which creates formatter instances using `SubstitutionFormatStringUtils`\\n- File logger writes formatted output directly to disk\\n\\n#### 2. Stream Loggers (envoy.access_loggers.stdout/stderr)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/stream/config.cc`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/stream/v3/stream.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured)\\n- Stdout/Stderr loggers support `log_format` (SubstitutionFormatString)\\n- JSON formatting possible through SubstitutionFormatString configuration\\n- Implemented via `StdoutAccessLogFactory` and `StderrAccessLogFactory`\\n\\n#### 3. gRPC Access Log Service (ALS) - HTTP (envoy.access_loggers.http_grpc)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/http_config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/http_grpc_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/v3/als.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured via Protocol Buffers)\\n- HTTP gRPC access logger sends HTTP request/response data via gRPC\\n- Supports custom tags (type.tracing.v3.CustomTag) for additional structured fields\\n- Implemented via `HttpGrpcAccessLogFactory`\\n- Proto includes HTTPRequestProperties and HTTPResponseProperties with headers/trailers\\n- Structured logging through protocol buffer messages to remote gRPC service\\n\\n#### 4. gRPC Access Log Service (ALS) - TCP (envoy.access_loggers.tcp_grpc)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/tcp_config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/tcp_grpc_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/grpc/v3/als.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured via Protocol Buffers)\\n- TCP gRPC access logger sends TCP connection data via gRPC\\n- Uses CommonGrpcAccessLogConfig with streaming and custom tags\\n- Implemented via `TcpGrpcAccessLogFactory`\\n- Structured logging through protocol buffer messages\\n\\n#### 5. Fluentd Logger (envoy.access_loggers.fluentd)\\n**Location:** `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/config.cc` and `source/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/fluentd_access_log_impl.h`\\n**Proto:** `envoy/extensions/access_loggers/fluentd/v3/fluentd.proto`\\n**JSON Support:** YES (Structured)\\n- Sends logs to Fluentd via Forward Protocol over TCP\\n- Uses JSON formatter internally (`SubstitutionFormatStringUtils::createJsonFormatter`)\\n- Converts JSON to MessagePack for Fluentd wire format\\n- Supports nested JSON objects through `google.protobuf.Struct record` field\\n- Configured via `FluentdAccessLogFactory`\\n- Field: `record` is a Struct containing formatted fields rendered as strings, numbers, or booleans\\n\\n#### 6. Filters are not sink implementations but determine whether logs are emitted:\\n\\n#### 1. StatusCodeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on HTTP response status code comparison\\n- Supports: GE, EQ, LE operations\\n\\n#### 2. DurationFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on request/response duration comparison\\n- Supports: GE, EQ, LE operations\\n\\n#### 3. NotHealthCheckFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters out Envoy health check requests\\n\\n#### 4. TraceableRequestFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters traceable requests only\\n\\n#### 5. RuntimeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on runtime configuration and fractional percentages\\n\\n#### 6. AndFilter / OrFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Composite filters combining multiple filters with AND/OR logic\\n\\n#### 7. HeaderFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on HTTP header matching\\n\\n#### 8. ResponseFlagFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on Envoy response flags\\n\\n#### 9. GrpcStatusFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on gRPC status codes\\n- Can infer gRPC status from HTTP status codes\\n\\n#### 10. LogTypeFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on access log type (HTTP, TCP)\\n\\n#### 11. MetadataFilter\\n**Location:** `source/common/access_log/access_log_impl.h`\\n- Filters based on dynamic metadata matching\\n\\n#### 12. WASM logger is extensible.\\n\\n2. **Formatting Infrastructure:** All sink implementations use the `SubstitutionFormatString` abstraction from `source/common/formatter/substitution_format_string.h` for consistent format handling.\\n\\n3. **Base Class Architecture:** All sink implementations inherit from `ImplBase` (in `source/extensions/access_loggers/common/access_log_base.h`), which handles filter evaluation and logging orchestration.\\n\\n4. **Filter Extensibility:** The system supports both built-in filters and extension filters via the `ExtensionFilterFactory` interface, allowing for custom filter implementations like CEL.\\n\\n5. **Common Configuration Pattern:** gRPC-based loggers (HTTP gRPC, TCP gRPC, OpenTelemetry) share common configuration patterns via `CommonGrpcAccessLogConfig` or similar structures, supporting batching, buffering, and custom tags.\\n\\n6. **Structured Data Support:** File, Fluentd, and OpenTelemetry loggers explicitly support structured data (nested objects, custom fields) through Protobuf Struct types and custom field mappings.\"\n}\n",
